The root cause is a multi-level compatibility problem where pandas nullable integers with NA values are forcibly converted to `float64` arrays, breaking expectations of downstream libraries that anticipate integer data types.\n\n---\n\n## Problem Overview\n\n### Symptom\n```python\nimport pandas as pd\nfrom sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler\n\ndf = pd.DataFrame({'x': pd.array([1, 2, None], dtype=\"Int64\")})\nscaler = StandardScaler()\nscaler.fit(df)  # May fail or produce unexpected results\n```\n\n### Root Cause Chain\nThe issue spans three conversion layers:\n1. **pandas dtype inference** - Forces float64 conversion\n2. **Array interface protocol** - Fails with NA values\n3. **NumPy array construction** - No native ExtensionDtype support\n\n---\n\n## Detailed Root Cause Analysis\n\n### Layer 1: Automatic Type Inference in `to_numpy_dtype_inference()`\n\n**Location**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/_utils.py` (Lines 27-75)\n\n**Root Cause Code** (Lines 35-45):\n```python\nif dtype is None and is_numeric_dtype(arr.dtype):\n    inferred_numeric_dtype = True\n    if hasna:\n        if arr.dtype.kind == \"b\":\n            result_dtype = np.dtype(np.object_)\n        else:\n            if arr.dtype.kind in \"iu\":            # INTEGER or UNSIGNED\n                result_dtype = np.dtype(np.float64)  # ← PROBLEM: Converts int to float64\n            else:\n                result_dtype = arr.dtype.numpy_dtype\n            if na_value is lib.no_default:\n                if not is_nan_na():\n                    na_value = NA\n                    dtype = np.dtype(object)\n                else:\n                    na_value = np.nan  # ← float64 uses NaN for missing\n```\n\n**Why This Is a Problem**:\n- When `dtype=None` (the default for most library calls), pandas automatically infers that nullable integers with NA values should become `float64`\n- This happens even if there's only a single NA value in the entire array\n- scikit-learn preprocessing functions don't explicitly specify dtype, triggering this automatic conversion\n- The resulting `float64` array is incompatible with operations expecting integer dtypes\n\n**Validation Layer** (Lines 70-75):\n```python\nif inferred_numeric_dtype and hasna:\n    try:\n        np_can_hold_element(result_dtype, na_value)  # Validates NA compatibility\n    except LossySetitemError:\n        result_dtype = np.dtype(np.object_)\nreturn result_dtype, na_value\n```\n\nThe validation at line 72 ensures `np.nan` (float) can be used as a NA value. For integer dtypes, `np.nan` is not valid, so float64 becomes the fallback.\n\n---\n\n### Layer 2: Array Protocol Failure in `__array__()`\n\n**Location**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/masked.py` (Lines 694-716)\n\n**Problematic Code** (Lines 701-712):\n```python\ndef __array__(self, dtype: NpDtype | None = None, copy: bool | None = None) -> np.ndarray:\n    \"\"\"\n    the array interface, return my values\n    We return an object array here to preserve our scalar values\n    \"\"\"\n    if copy is False:\n        if not self._hasna:\n            # ← PROBLEM: Fails when NA values present\n            \"Unable to avoid copy while creating an array as requested.\"\n        )\n\n    if copy is None:\n        copy = False\n    return self.to_numpy(dtype=dtype, copy=copy)\n```\n\n**Why This Is a Problem**:\n- NumPy's array protocol calls `__array__()` to convert objects to arrays\n- When NA values are present and `copy=False` is requested (common optimization), a `ValueError` is raised\n- This breaks libraries that assume they can efficiently access array data\n- Fallback to `to_numpy()` triggers the type inference issue from Layer 1\n\n---\n\n### Layer 3: Forced Conversion in `to_numpy()`\n\n**Location**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/masked.py` (Lines 512-606)\n\n**Problematic Code** (Lines 578-606):\n```python\ndef to_numpy(\n    self,\n    dtype: npt.DTypeLike | None = None,\n    copy: bool = False,\n    na_value: object = lib.no_default,\n) -> np.ndarray:\n    # hold Python `pd.NA`\n   - `float64` dtype to use `np.nan` as NA sentinel\n\n2. **NumPy limitation**: No native NA/missing value support in integer dtypes\n   - NumPy integers cannot natively represent NA\n   - NumPy float64 uses special `np.nan` value for NA\n\n3. **Integer array storage**: pandas nullable integers actually store:\n   - `_data`: int64 array (no NA space)\n   - `_mask`: bool array (NA positions)\n\n4. **Conversion conflict**: When converting to single NumPy array:\n   - Cannot preserve integer dtype with NA values\n   - Must choose: lose integer info (→ float64) OR lose NA positions (→ object)\n\n---\n\n## Breaking Point Details\n\n### Scenario 1: Default Library Behavior\n```python\ndf = pd.DataFrame({'x': pd.array([1, 2, None], dtype=\"Int64\")})\narr = The root cause is a multi-level compatibility problem where pandas nullable integers with NA values are forcibly converted to `float64` arrays, breaking expectations of downstream libraries that anticipate integer data types.\n\n---\n\n## Problem Overview\n\n### Symptom\n```python\nimport pandas as pd\nfrom sklearn.preprocessing import StandardScaler\n\ndf = pd.DataFrame({'x': pd.array([1, 2, None], dtype=\"Int64\")})\nscaler = StandardScaler()\nscaler.fit(df)  # May fail or produce unexpected results\n```\n\n### Root Cause Chain\nThe issue spans three conversion layers:\n1. **pandas dtype inference** - Forces float64 conversion\n2. **Array interface protocol** - Fails with NA values\n3. **NumPy array construction** - No native ExtensionDtype support\n\n---\n\n## Detailed Root Cause Analysis\n\n### Layer 1: Automatic Type Inference in `to_numpy_dtype_inference()`\n\n**Location**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/_utils.py` (Lines 27-75)\n\n**Root Cause Code** (Lines 35-45):\n```python\nif dtype is None and is_numeric_dtype(arr.dtype):\n    inferred_numeric_dtype = True\n    if hasna:\n        if arr.dtype.kind == \"b\":\n            result_dtype = np.dtype(np.object_)\n        else:\n            if arr.dtype.kind in \"iu\":            # INTEGER or UNSIGNED\n                result_dtype = np.dtype(np.float64)  # ← PROBLEM: Converts int to float64\n            else:\n                result_dtype = arr.dtype.numpy_dtype\n            if na_value is lib.no_default:\n                if not is_nan_na():\n                    na_value = NA\n                    dtype = np.dtype(object)\n                else:\n                    na_value = np.nan  # ← float64 uses NaN for missing\n```\n\n**Why This Is a Problem**:\n- When `dtype=None` (the default for most library calls), pandas automatically infers that nullable integers with NA values should become `float64`\n- This happens even if there's only a single NA value in the entire array\n- scikit-learn preprocessing functions don't explicitly specify dtype, triggering this automatic conversion\n- The resulting `float64` array is incompatible with operations expecting integer dtypes\n\n**Validation Layer** (Lines 70-75):\n```python\nif inferred_numeric_dtype and hasna:\n    try:\n        np_can_hold_element(result_dtype, na_value)  # Validates NA compatibility\n    except LossySetitemError:\n        result_dtype = np.dtype(np.object_)\nreturn result_dtype, na_value\n```\n\nThe validation at line 72 ensures `np.nan` (float) can be used as a NA value. For integer dtypes, `np.nan` is not valid, so float64 becomes the fallback.\n\n---\n\n### Layer 2: Array Protocol Failure in `__array__()`\n\n**Location**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/masked.py` (Lines 694-716)\n\n**Problematic Code** (Lines 701-712):\n```python\ndef __array__(self, dtype: NpDtype | None = None, copy: bool | None = None) -> np.ndarray:\n    \"\"\"\n    the array interface, return my values\n    We return an object array here to preserve our scalar values\n    \"\"\"\n    if copy is False:\n        if not self._hasna:\n            # ← PROBLEM: Fails when NA values present\n            \"Unable to avoid copy while creating an array as requested.\"\n        )\n\n    if copy is None:\n        copy = False\n    return self.to_numpy(dtype=dtype, copy=copy)\n```\n\n**Why This Is a Problem**:\n- NumPy's array protocol calls `__array__()` to convert objects to arrays\n- When NA values are present and `copy=False` is requested (common optimization), a `ValueError` is raised\n- This breaks libraries that assume they can efficiently access array data\n- Fallback to `to_numpy()` triggers the type inference issue from Layer 1\n\n---\n\n### Layer 3: Forced Conversion in `to_numpy()`\n\n**Location**: `/ccb_crossrepo/src/pandas/pandas/core/arrays/masked.py` (Lines 512-606)\n\n**Problematic Code** (Lines 578-606):\n```python\ndef to_numpy(\n    self,\n    dtype: npt.DTypeLike | None = None,\n    copy: bool = False,\n    na_value: object = lib.no_default,\n) -> np.ndarray:\n    # data\n```\n\n**Why This Is a Problem**:\n- Line 579: Calls `to_numpy_dtype_inference()` which returns `float64` for Int64 arrays with NA\n- Line 597: Calls `astype(dtype)` which converts the
